For fiscal 2026, revenue was $215.9 billion, up 65% from a year ago.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">For the quarter, GAAP and non-GAAP gross margins were 75.0% and 75.2%, respectively. Grace Blackwell with NVLink is the king of inference today &#8212; delivering an order-of-magnitude lower cost per token &#8212; and Vera Rubin will extend that leadership even further,&#8221; said Jensen Huang, founder and CEO of NVIDIA. &#8220;Enterprise adoption of agents is skyrocketing. Our customers are racing to invest in AI compute &#8212; the factories powering the AI industrial revolution and their future growth.&#8221;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">During fiscal 2026, NVIDIA returned $41.1 billion to shareholders in the form of shares repurchased and cash dividends. The reconciliations for fiscal years 2025 and 2026 adjust the related GAAP financial measures to exclude stock-based compensation expense, acquisition-related and other costs, other, gains&#47;losses from non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities, net, interest expense related to amortization of debt discount, and the associated tax impact of these items where applicable. Our platforms address four large markets where our expertise is critical&#58; Data Center, Gaming, Professional Visualization, and Automotive.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;margin-top:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Revenue</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Revenue for the fourth quarter was a record $68.1 billion, up 73% from a year ago and up 20% sequentially. Fiscal year revenue was a record $215.9 billion, up 65% from a year ago.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Data Center revenue for the fourth quarter was a record $62.3 billion, up 75% from a year ago and up 22% sequentially, driven by the major platform shifts &#8211; accelerated computing and AI.  For the fourth quarter, hyperscaler revenue increased and remained our largest customer category at slightly over 50% of Data Center revenue, while growth was led by the rest of our Data Center customers as revenue diversified.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Data Center compute revenue was a record $51.3 billion, up 58% from a year ago and up 19% sequentially. Networking revenue was a record $11.0 billion, up 263% from a year ago and up 34% sequentially from the introduction and continued ramp of NVLink&#8482; compute fabric for GB200 and GB300 systems and the growth of Ethernet and InfiniBand platforms.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Gaming revenue for the fourth quarter was up 47% from a year ago, driven by strong Blackwell demand. Gaming revenue was down 13% sequentially as channel inventory naturally moderated following a season of strong holiday demand. We expect supply constraints to be a headwind to Gaming in the first quarter of fiscal 2027 and beyond.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Professional Visualization revenue for the fourth quarter was up 159% from a year ago and up 74% sequentially, driven by exceptional demand for Blackwell.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Automotive revenue for the fourth quarter was up 6% from a year ago and up 2% sequentially, driven by continued adoption of our self-driving platforms.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;margin-top:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Gross Margin</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP and non-GAAP gross margins for the fourth quarter increased from a year ago on lower inventory provisions. GAAP and non-GAAP gross margins increased sequentially as Blackwell continued to ramp with an improved mix and cost structure.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;margin-top:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Expenses</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP operating expenses for the fourth quarter were up 45% from a year ago and up 16% sequentially, and non-GAAP operating expenses were up 51% from a year ago and up 21% </font></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:42.75pt;width:100%"><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">sequentially. The fourth quarter GAAP increases from a year ago were driven by higher compensation and benefits expense due to employee growth, and compute and infrastructure costs. The non-GAAP increases were driven by compute and infrastructure costs and compensation and benefits. The fourth quarter GAAP and non-GAAP sequential increase was driven by engineering development materials for new product introductions and compute and infrastructure costs.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;margin-top:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Other Income &#38; Expense and Income Tax</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP other income and expense (OI&#38;E) includes interest income, interest expense, and unrealized non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities gains or losses. Non-GAAP OI&#38;E excludes unrealized non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities gains or losses.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Interest income for the fourth quarter was $568 million, up from a year ago and down sequentially, driven by changes in cash, cash equivalents, and debt securities. Net other income for the fourth quarter was $5.6 billion, driven by unrealized gains in non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities, including gains from our previously announced investment in Intel&#8217;s common stock.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP effective tax rate for the fourth quarter and fiscal year was 14.8% and 15.1%, respectively, an increase from a year ago primarily due to a lower impact from stock-based compensation tax benefits. Non-GAAP effective tax rate for the fourth quarter and fiscal year was 15.4% and 16.1%, respectively.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;margin-top:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Balance Sheet and Cash Flow</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Cash, cash equivalents and marketable securities were $62.6 billion, up from $43.2 billion a year ago and $60.6 billion a quarter ago. The increases primarily reflect higher revenue, partially offset by outlays for an intellectual property license, strategic investments and stock repurchases.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Accounts receivable was $38.5 billion with 51 days sales outstanding (DSO), down from 53 days sequentially, driven by timing of cash collections.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Inventory was $21.4 billion, up from $19.8 billion sequentially, and total supply-related commitments were $95.2 billion. We have strategically secured inventory and capacity to meet demand beyond the next several quarters.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Multi-year cloud service agreements were $27.0 billion, up from $26.0 billion sequentially, to support the growing needs of our research and development efforts.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Cash flow from operating activities was $36.2 billion, up from $16.6 billion a year ago and up from $23.8 billion a quarter ago. The year-on-year and sequential increases reflect growth in revenue.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We returned $4.1 billion to shareholders in the fourth quarter through $3.8 billion of share repurchases and $243 million of cash dividends. In fiscal 2026, we returned $41.1 billion to shareholders through $40.1 billion of share repurchases and $974 million of cash dividends.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:6pt;margin-top:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Outlook</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Beginning in the first quarter of fiscal 2027, we will include stock-based compensation expense in our non-GAAP financial measures. Stock-based compensation is a foundational component of our compensation program to attract and retain world-class talent.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Outlook for the first quarter of fiscal 2027 is as follows&#58;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;padding-left:36pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;padding-left:13.89pt">Revenue is expected to be $78.0 billion, plus or minus 2%. We are not assuming any Data Center compute revenue from China in our outlook.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;padding-left:36pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;padding-left:13.89pt">GAAP and non-GAAP gross margins are expected to be 74.9% and 75.0%, respectively, plus or minus 50 basis points, inclusive of a 0.1% impact from stock-based compensation expense.</font></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div material changes to our tax environment.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Non-GAAP Measures</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">To supplement NVIDIA&#8217;s condensed consolidated financial statements presented in accordance with GAAP, the company uses non-GAAP measures of certain components of financial performance. These non-GAAP measures include non-GAAP gross profit, non-GAAP gross margin, non-GAAP operating expenses, non-GAAP operating income, non-GAAP other income (expense), net, non-GAAP net income, non-GAAP net income, or earnings, per diluted share, and free cash flow. For NVIDIA&#8217;s investors to be better able to compare its current results with those of previous periods, the company has shown a reconciliation of GAAP to non-GAAP financial measures. The reconciliations for fiscal years 2025 and 2026 adjust the related GAAP financial measures to exclude stock-based compensation expense, acquisition-related and other costs, other, gains&#47;losses from non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities, net, interest expense related to amortization of debt discount, and the associated tax impact of these items where applicable. Beginning in the first quarter of fiscal 2027, NVIDIA&#8217;s non-GAAP financial measures will no longer exclude stock-based compensation expense. Free cash flow is calculated as GAAP net cash provided by operating activities less both purchases related to property and equipment and intangible assets and principal payments on property and equipment and intangible assets. NVIDIA believes the presentation of its non-GAAP financial measures enhances the user's overall understanding of the company&#8217;s historical financial performance. The presentation of the company&#8217;s non-GAAP financial measures is not meant to be considered in isolation or as a substitute for the company&#8217;s financial results prepared in accordance with GAAP, and the company&#8217;s non-GAAP measures may be different from non-GAAP measures used by other companies.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:9pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Certain statements in this CFO Commentary including, but not limited to, statements as to&#58; expectations with respect to growth, performance and benefits of our products, services, and technologies, including Blackwell, and related trends and drivers&#59; expectations with respect to supply and demand for our products, services, and technologies, including Blackwell, and related matters including inventory, production and distribution&#59; expectations with respect to our third party arrangements, including with its collaborators and partners&#59; expectations with respect to technology developments, including Vera Rubin, and related trends and drivers&#59; our future cash dividends or other returns to stockholders, our financial and business outlook for the first quarter of fiscal 2027 and beyond&#59; projected market growth and trends&#59; expectations with respect to AI and related industries&#59; and other statements that are not historical facts are forward-looking statements within the meaning of Section 27A of the Securities Act of 1933, as amended, and Section 21E of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, which are subject to the &#8220;safe harbor&#8221; created by those sections based on management&#8217;s beliefs and assumptions and on information currently available to management and are subject to risks and uncertainties that could cause results to be materially different than expectations.
